               )\n   428→                return loop_idx < map_length\n   429→\n   430→            def body_fn(*flat_args):\n   431→                loop_idx, out_bufs, xs, additional_inputs = raise AssertionError(\"map is not lowered to while_loop\")\n   471→\n   472→\n   473→def resolve_shape_to_proxy(\n   474→    shape: list[int | torch.SymInt], bound_symbols: dict[Any, Any]\n   475→):\n   476→    \"\"\"\n   477→    Given a list of symints/ints, this function returns a calculated expression of bound_symbols' values.\n   478→    When we trace this function, we'll get a graph with call_function nodes that describes how the shape expr is\n   479→    computed from bound_symbols' values.\n   480→\n   481→    Suppose shape = (s1*s2, s1+s2) and bound_symbols = {s1: arg0, s2: arg1}, the result will be\n   482→    (arg0 * arg1, arg0 + arg1).\n   483→    \"\"\"\n   484→    from torch.utils._sympy.interp import sympy_interp\n   485→    from torch.utils._sympy.reference import PythonReferenceAnalysis\n   486→\n   487→    ret = []\n   488→    for s in shape:\n   489→        if isinstance(s, torch.SymInt):\n   490→            ret.append(\n   491→                sympy_interp(\n   492→                    PythonReferenceAnalysis,\n   493→                    bound_symbols,\n   494→                    s.node.expr,\n   495→                ),\n   496→            )\n   497→        else:\n   498→            assert isinstance(s, int)\n   499→            ret.append(s)\n   500→    return ret\n   501→\n   502→\n   503→def decompose_scan_to_while_loop(gm: torch.fx.GraphModule):\n   504→    \"\"\"\n   505→    NOTE [decompose scan to while_loop]\n   506→    This pass decomposes `scan` to  `while_loop` by replacing the scan fx_node with a while_loop hop.\n   507→\n   508→    Suppose we have a function f:\n   509→\n   510→        def f():\n   511→            init = torch.zeros([])\n   512→            xs = torch.arange(4)\n   513→            ys = []\n   514→            for i in range(xs.size(0)):\n   515→                init = xs[i] + init\n   516→                ys.append(init)\n   517→\n   518→            # Return the final carry and stack the intermediates\n   519→            return init, torch.stack(ys)\n   520→\n   521→    We could rewrite it with a scan with the benefits of reducing compilation time/binary size, reducing\n   522→    memory usage, supporting loops over unbacked shapes and cudagraph etc.\n   523→\n   524→        def g():\n   525→            def step_fn(init: torch.Tensor, x: torch.Tensor):\n   526→                next_init = x + init\n   527→                return next_init, next_init\n   528→\n   529→            init = torch.zeros([])\n   530→            xs = torch.arange(4)\n   531→            final_carry, ys = torch._higher_order.scan(step_fn, init, xs)\n   532→            return final_carry, ys\n   533→\n   534→    This pass will rewrite scan into:\n   535→\n   536→        def k():\n   537→            init = torch.zeros([])\n   538→            xs = torch.arange(4)\n   539→\n   540→            # we create a loop_idx and loop through xs.shape[0]\n   541→            loop_idx = torch.zeros([])\n   542→            ys = torch.empty_strided(_shape_stride_of_ys)\n   543→            def cond_fn(loop_idx, ys, init, xs):\n   544→                return loop_idx < xs.shape[0]\n   545→\n   546→            # we pre-allocate the output buffer ys and inplace\n   547→            # copy the y of each intermediate into a slice.\n   548→            # NOTE [Pre-allocate scan's output buffer].\n   549→            def body_fn(loop_idx, ys, init, xs):\n   550→                int_idx = loop_idx.item()\n   551→                next_init, y = step_fn(init, xs[int_idx])\n   552→                ys[int_idx].copy_(y)\n   553→                return loop_idx + 1, ys, next_init, xs\n   554→\n   555→            final_carry, _, _, ys = torch._higher_order.while_loop(cond_fn, body_fn, (loop_idx, ys, init, xs))\n   556→            return final_carry, ys\n   557→    \"\"\"\n   558→\n   559→    graph_pass = PatternMatcherPass()\n   560→\n   561→    @register_graph_pattern(\n   562→        CallFunctionVarArgs(torch.ops.higher_order.scan),\n   563→        # pyrefly: ignore [bad-argument-type]\n   564→        pass_dict=graph_pass,\n   565→    )\n   566→    def _(match: Match, *args, **kwargs):\n   567→        from torch._higher_order_ops.scan import _extract_carry_and_out\n   568→\n   569→        assert len(kwargs) == 0, (\n   570→            \"kwargs of scan are not merged into args before entering decompose_scan_to_while_loop_pass\"\n   571→        )\n   572→\n   573→        combine_subgraph, fx_init, fx_xs, fx_additional_inputs = args\n   574→        assert combine_subgraph.op == \"get_attr\", \"first arg is not combine_subgraph\"\n   575→        sub_gm: torch.fx.GraphModule = getattr(gm, combine_subgraph.target)\n   576→        cur_node = match.nodes[0]\n   577→        num_init_leaves = len(fx_init)\n   578→        _, ys_outputs = _extract_carry_and_out(cur_node.meta[\"val\"], num_init_leaves)\n   579→\n   580→        def lower_to_while_loop(*args, **kwargs):\n   581→            \"\"\"\n   582→            The traced graph of this function will be used to replace the original scan fx_node.\n   583→            \"\"\"\n   584→            assert len(kwargs) == 0\n   585→\n   586→            # Step 1: construct necessary inputs to while_loop based on scan's input.\n   587→            (\n   588→                init,\n   589→                xs,\n   590→                additional_inputs,\n   591→            ) = pytree.tree_unflatten(args, tree_spec)\n   592→            scan_length = xs[0].size(0)\n   593→            loop_idx = torch.zeros([], dtype=torch.int64, device=torch.device(\"cpu\"))\n   594→\n   595→            # NOTE [Pre-allocate scan's output buffer]\n   596→            # In order to pre-allocate the output buffer for ys, we rely on the meta of scan's fx_node.\n   597→            # However, the meta consists of concrete symints, we need to bind those symints with\n   598→            # proxies in 1428→def is_valid_cat_splitwithsizes(match):\n  1429→    cat_nodes = filter_nodes(match.nodes, aten.cat)\n  1430→    split_nodes = filter_nodes(match.nodes, aten.split_with_sizes)\n  1431→    if In this case we can not manually pick the place for bucketed collective insertion.\n        # But we are guaranteed by the bucketing (independent collectives in the bucket),\n        # that it is possible to reorder nodes to satisfy all ordering requirements.\n        #\n        # torch.distributed.is_available():\n\n        def check():\n            # This is a wait node, and `other_node`` is some collective node.\n            # Eager semantics allow waits to be issued in a different order than\n            # the collectives. Reordering this wait node might reorder collectives\n            # which cause hangs. Once we have SPMD mode, we can safely reorder them.\n            # However, increasing the locality between a collective and its wait node\n            # is generally worse for performance.\n            return node.target != torch.ops._c10d_functional.wait_tensor.default\n    else:\n\n        def check():\n            return True\n\n    def visit(other_node):\n        if (\n            other_node.op == \"call_function\"\n            and other_node.target != operator.getitem\n            and all((n in seen_nodes) for n in other_node.users)\n            and get_mutation_region_id(graph, node)\n            == get_mutation_region_id(graph, other_node)\n            and check()\n        ):\n            # user1(wait_ag1)\n        #\n        # --- after bucketing ---\n        #\n        # in0 = ...\n        # user(wait_ag0) <--- wait_ag0 is defined only after bucketed collective.\n        #\n        # pre_in1 = ...\n        # in1 = transform(pre_in1)\n        # ag_bucket(in0+in1)\n        # wait_bucket\n        # wait_ag0 = wait_bucket[0]\n        # wait_ag1 = wait_bucket[1]\n        # user1(wait_ag1)\n        stable_topological_sort(gm.graph)\n\n    # torch.ops.aten.slice_scatter.default,\n        )\n\n    def is_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        node_device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        return node_device is not None and node_device.type == self.target\n\n    def is_cpu_scalar_tensor(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is a cpu scalar tensor.\n        \"\"\"\n        device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        is_cpu = device is not None and device.type == \"cpu\"\n        ten = node.meta.get(\"val\")\n        is_scalar = isinstance(ten, torch.Tensor) and len(ten.size()) == 0\n        return is_cpu and is_scalar\n\n    def all_inputs_are_cpu_scalar_or_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node's inputs are either cpu scalar tensors or\n        on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        inputs = (\n            inp\n target device.\n\n        If this function returns False, it means that this node and all of its users\n        won't be moved into the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        if node.target == def test_addmm_alpha_beta_with_pointwise(self):\n        # Test that addmm with alpha/beta != 1 is unfused correctly with pointwise ops\n        # See
